<<PARAGRAPH>>T ANK  I NSPECTION , R EPAIR , A LTERATION ,  AND  R ECONSTRUCTION
B-15<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>B.3.4.6
The edge settlement limits described in B.2.3.1 through B.2.3.4 were developed for typical  1 / 4 -in. thick tank
bottoms with minimal corrosion.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Edge settlement limits can be applied with reasonable accuracy to  5 / 16 - and  3 / 8 -in. thick tank bottoms.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Edge settlement limits can be applied with reasonable accuracy to bottoms with general corrosion, as long as the
areas near all welds are thicker than  3 / 16  in.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Edge settlement limits can be applied with reasonable accuracy to bottoms with local corrosion, if all locally thin
areas in the settled area (closer than “ R ” to the shell) thinner than  3 / 16  in. are smaller than 12 inches in diameter
and the thin area does not include a weld.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Settlement is presumed to be slow, and a small amount of additional settlement is expected to occur prior to the
next inspection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>B.3.4.7
Edge settlement increases secondary stress at the bottom-to-shell weld. If weld repairs are made to the
bottom-to-shell weld in an area where settlement exceeds  1 / 2  of  B e , these additional stresses should be evaluated by
an engineer experienced in tank settlement evaluation before waiving a hydrostatic test per 12.3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>B.4
Repairs<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>B.4.1
If it is determined that settlements have occurred which are beyond the permissible limits established in the
previous sections, then consideration should be given to making repairs or a rigorous stress analysis should be
performed to evaluate the deformed profile. Various repair techniques have been discussed above. The judgment
on repairs should be tempered with knowledge of tank service history, previous repairs, previous inspections, tank
foundation conditions, soil characteristics, the material of construction, and estimates of future settlement. See
9.10 for suggested repair details.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Settled
area<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Angle
alpha<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Tank
centerline<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Bottom plate
layout<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Figure B.13—Edge Settlement with a Lap Weld at an Arbitrary Angle to the Shell<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_112>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>B-16
API S TANDARD  653<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>B.4.2
For tanks with edge settlement exceeding the limits and assumptions given in B.2.3.1 through B.2.3.7,
the tank should be repaired. Any plate exceeding acceptable strains (typically 2 % to 3 %) should be replaced.
Re-leveling the tank will not remove the plastic strain, so leveling the tank without replacing the strain may not be
a sufficient repair. Welds in the area of the high strains should be removed and replaced, or be subjected to a
fitness-for-service evaluation by an engineer experienced in tank settlement evaluation. The condition leading to
the unacceptable settlement should be corrected. Depending on the severity and location of the settlement,
required repairs may include regrading the soil under the tank bottom, and/or repairing the foundation. Jacking
and re-leveling the shell may be required to prevent additional settlement damage. Jacking and leveling are
usually done in conjunction with, not instead of, replacing damaged plate and welds. In lieu of repairs, a detailed
analysis of the settled area may be performed by an engineer experienced in tank design and settlement
evaluation. The analysis should consider primary and secondary stress and the risk of brittle fracture.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=2>>Annex C
(informative)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=2>>Checklists for Tank Inspection<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Annex C contains sample checklists illustrating tank components and auxiliary items that should be considered for
internal and external inspection of tanks. This information is provided as guidance to the owner/operator for
developing an inspection assessment schedule for any specific tank installation. The checklist format facilitates the
recording of inspection findings.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1
Users of checklists should not rely exclusively on the information contained in this document. Sound business,
scientific, engineering, and safety judgment should be used in employing the information contained herein.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
Where applicable, authorities having jurisdiction should be consulted.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>T ANK  I NSPECTION , R EPAIR , A LTERATION ,  AND  R ECONSTRUCTION
C-3<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Tank In-service Inspection Checklist<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Item
Completed<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Comments<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.1
Foundation<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Measure foundation levelness and bottom elevations (see Annex B for extent of
measurements).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.1.1
Concrete Ring<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect for broken concrete, spalling, and cracks, particularly under backup bars used
in welding butt-welded annular rings under the shell.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Inspect drain openings in ring, back of waterdraw basins and top surface of ring for
indications of bottom leakage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Inspect for cavities under foundation and vegetation against bottom of tank.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Check that runoff rainwater from the shell drains away from tank.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Check for settlement around perimeter of tank.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.1.2
Asphalt<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Check for settling of tank into asphalt base which would direct runoff rain water under
the tank instead of away from it.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Look for areas where leaching of oil has left rock filler exposed, which indicates
hydrocarbon leakage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.1.3
Oiled Dirt or Sand<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Check for settlement into the base which would direct runoff rain water under the tank
rather than away from it.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.1.4
Rock<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Presence of crushed rock under the steel bottom usually results in severe underside
corrosion. Make a note to do additional bottom plate examination (ultrasonic, hammer
testing, or turning of coupons) when the tank is out of service.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.1.5
Site Drainage<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Check site for drainage away from the tank and associated piping and manifolds.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Check operating condition of the dike drains.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.1.6
Housekeeping<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Inspect the area for buildup of trash, vegetation, and other inflammables buildup.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.1.7
Cathodic Protection<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Review cathodic protection potential readings.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.2
Shells<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.2.1
External Visual Inspection<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Visually inspect for paint failures, pitting, and corrosion.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Clean off the bottom angle area and inspect for corrosion and thinning on plate and
weld.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Inspect the bottom-to-foundation seal, if any.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.2.2
Internal (Floating Roof Tank)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Visually inspect for grooving, corrosion, pitting, and coating failures.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.2.3
Riveted Shell Inspection<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect external surface for rivet and seam leaks.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Locate leaks by sketch or photo (location will be lost when shell is abrasive cleaned
for painting).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Inspect rivets for corrosion loss and wear.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Inspect vertical seams to see if they have been full fillet lap-welded to increase joint
efficiency.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.2.4
Wind Girder (Floating Roof Tanks)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect wind girder and handrail for corrosion damage (paint failure, pitting, corrosion
product buildup), especially where it occurs at tack-welded junction, and for broken
welds.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Check support welds to shell for pitting, especially on shell plates.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Note whether supports have reinforcing pads welded to shell.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.3
Shell Appurtenances<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.3.1
Manways and Nozzles<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect for cracks or signs of leakage on weld joint at nozzles, manways, and
reinforcing plates.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Inspect for shell plate dimpling around nozzles, caused by excessive pipe deflection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Inspect for flange leaks and leaks around bolting.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Inspect sealing of insulation around manways and nozzles.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Check for inadequate manway flange and cover thickness on mixer manways.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.3.2
Tank Piping Manifolds<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect manifold piping, flanges, and valves for leaks.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Inspect fire fighting system components.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Check for anchored piping which would be hazardous to the tank shell or bottom
connections during earth movement.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Check for adequate thermal pressure relief of piping to the tank.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Check operation of regulators for tanks with purge gas systems.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
Check sample connections for leaks and for proper valve operation.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) Check for damage and test the accuracy of temperature indicators.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h) Check welds on shell-mounted davit clips above valves 6 in. and larger.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.3.3
Autogauge System<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect autogauge tape guide and lower sheave housing (floating swings) for leaks.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Inspect autogauge head for damage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Bump the checker on autogauge head for proper movement of tape.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Identify size and construction material of autogauge tape guide (floating roof tanks).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Ask operator if tape tends to hang up during tank roof movement (floating roof tanks).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
Compare actual product level to the reading on the autogauge (maximum variation is
2 in.).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) On floating roof tanks, when the roof is in the lowest position, check that no more than
two ft of tape are exposed at the end of the tape guide.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h) Inspect condition of board and legibility of board-type autogauges.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>i)
Test freedom of movement of marker and float.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.3.4
Shell-mounted Sample Station<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect sample lines for function of valves and plugging of lines, including drain or
return-to-tank line.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Check circulation pump for leaks and operating problems.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>T ANK  I NSPECTION , R EPAIR , A LTERATION ,  AND  R ECONSTRUCTION
C-5<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Tank In-service Inspection Checklist (Continued)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Item
Completed<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Comments<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Test bracing and supports for sample lines and equipment.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.3.5
Heater (Shell Manway Mounted)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Inspect condensate drain for presence of oil indicating leakage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.3.6
Mixer<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect for proper mounting flange and support.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Inspect for leakage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Inspect condition of power lines and connections to mixer.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.3.7
Swing Lines: Winch Operation<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Nonfloating. Raise, then lower the swing line with the winch, and check for cable
tightness to confirm that swing line lowered properly.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Floating. With tank half full or more, lower the swing line, then let out cable and check
if swing has pulled cable tight, indicating that the winch is operating properly.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Indicator. Check that the indicator moves in the proper direction: Floating swing line
indicators show a lower level as cable is wound up on the winch. Non-floating swing
line indicators show the opposite.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.3.8
Swing Lines: External Guide System<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Check for leaks at threaded and flanged joints.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.3.9
Swing Lines: Identify Ballast Varying Need<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Check for significant difference in stock specific gravity.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.3.10
Swing Lines: Cable Material and Condition<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) For nonstainless steel cable, check for corrosion over entire length.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) All cable: check for wear or fraying.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.3.11
Swing Lines: Product Sample Comparison<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Check for water or gravity differences that would indicate a leaking swing joint.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.3.12
Swing Lines: Target<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Target should indicate direction of swing opening (up or down) and height above bottom
where suction will be lost with swing on bottom support.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.4
Roofs<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.4.1
Deck Plate Internal Corrosion<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For safety, before accessing the roof, check with ultrasonic instrument or lightly use a ball
peen hammer to test the deck plate near the edge of the roof for thinning. (Corrosion
normally attacks the deck plate at the edge of a fixed roof and at the rafters in the center
of the roof first.)<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.4.2
Deck Plate External Corrosion<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Visually inspect for paint failure, holes, pitting, and corrosion product on the roof deck.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.4.3
Roof Deck Drainage<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Look for indication of standing water. (Significant sagging of fixed roof deck indicates
potential rafter failure. Large standing water areas on a floating roof indicate inadequate
drainage design or, if to one side, a nonlevel roof with possible leaking pontoons.)<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.4.4
Level of Floating Roof<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>At several locations, measure distance from roof rim to a horizontal weld seam above the
roof. A variance in the readings indicates a nonlevel roof with possible shell out-of-round,
out-of-plumb, leaking pontoons, or hang-up. On small diameter tanks, an unlevel
condition can indicate unequal loading at that level.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>C-6
API S TANDARD  653<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Tank In-service Inspection Checklist (Continued)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Item
Completed<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Comments<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.4.5
Gas Test Internal Floating Roof<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Test for explosive gas on top of the internal floating roof. Readings could indicate a
leaking roof, leaking seal system, or inadequate ventilation of the area above the internal
floating roof.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.4.6
Roof Insulation<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Visually inspect for cracks or leaks in the insulation weather coat where runoff rain
water could penetrate the insulation.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Inspect for wet insulation under the weather coat.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Remove small test sections of insulation and check roof plate for corrosion and holes
near areas susceptible to water ingress (i.e. roof nozzles, etc.).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.4.7
Floating Roof Seal Systems<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect the condition of the seal, measure and record maximum rim spaces and seal-
to-shell gaps around the full roof circumference at the level of inspection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Inspection of the seal and measurement of the rim spaces and seal-to-shell
gaps at more than one level may be necessary to more fully determine if any
problems exist at other levels of tank operation).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Measure and record annular space at 30-ft spacing (minimum of four quadrants)
around roof and record. Measurements should be taken in directly opposite pairs.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1) _______ _______ Opposite pair 1.
2) _______ _______ Opposite pair 2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Check if seal fabric on primary shoe seals is pulling shoes away from shell (fabric not
wide enough).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Inspect fabric for deterioration, holes, tears, and cracks.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Inspect visible metallic parts for corrosion and wear.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
Inspect for openings in seals that would permit vapor emissions.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) Inspect for protruding bolt or rivet heads against the shell.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h) Pull both primary and secondary seal systems back all around the shell to check their
operation.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>i)
Inspect secondary seals for signs of buckling or indications that their angle with the
shell is too shallow.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>j)
Inspect wedge-type wiper seals for flexibility, resilience, cracks, and tears.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.5
Roof Appurtenances<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.5.1
Sample Hatch<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect condition and functioning of sample hatch cover.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) On tanks governed by Air Quality Monitoring District rules, check for the condition of
seal inside hatch cover.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Check for corrosion and plugging on thief and gauge hatch cover.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Where sample hatch is used to reel gauge stock level, check for marker and tab
stating hold-off distance.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Check for reinforcing pad where sample hatch pipe penetrates the roof deck.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
On floating roof sample hatch and recoil systems, inspect operation of recoil reel and
condition of rope.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) Test operation of system.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h) On ultra clean stocks such as JP4, check for presence and condition of protective
coating or liner inside sample hatch (preventing rust from pipe getting into sample).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>Tank In-service Inspection Checklist (Continued)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Item
Completed<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Comments<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.5.2
Gauge Well<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect visible portion of the gauge well for thinning, size of slots, and cover condition.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Check for a hold-off distance marker and tab with hold-off distance (legible).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) On floating roofs, inspect condition of roof guide for gauge well, particularly the
condition of the rollers for grooving.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) If accessible, check the distance from the gauge well pipe to the tank shell at different
levels.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) If tank has a gauge well washer, check valve for leakage and for presence of a bull
plug or blind flange.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.5.3
Fixed Roof Scaffold Support<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Inspect scaffold support for corrosion, wear, and structural soundness.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.5.4
Autogauge: Inspection Hatch and Guides (Fixed Roof)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Check the hatch for corrosion and missing bolts.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Look for corrosion on the tape guide’s and float guide’s wire anchors.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.5.5
Autogauge: Float Well Cover<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect for corrosion.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Check tape cable for wear or fraying caused by rubbing on the cover.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.5.6
Sample Hatch (Internal Floating Roof)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Check overall conditions.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) When equipped with a fabric seal, check for automatic sealing after sampling.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) When equipped with a recoil reel opening device, check for proper operations.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.5.7
Roof-mounted Vents (Internal Floating Roof)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Check condition of screens, locking and pivot pins.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.5.8
Gauging Platform Drip Ring<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>On fixed roof tanks with drip rings under the gauging platform or sampling area, inspect
for plugged drain return to the tank.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.5.9
Emergency Roof Drains<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Inspect vapor plugs for emergency drain: that seal fabric discs are slightly smaller than
the pipe ID and that fabric seal is above the liquid level.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.5.10
Removable Roof Leg Racks<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Check for leg racks on roof.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.5.11
Vacuum Breakers<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Report size, number, and type of vacuum breakers. Inspect vacuum breakers. If high legs
are set, check for setting of mechanical breaker in high leg position.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.5.12
Rim Vents<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Check condition of the screen on the rim vent cover.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Check for plating off or removal of rim vents where jurisdictional rules do not permit
removal.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1.5.13
Pontoon Inspection Hatches<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Open pontoon inspection hatch covers and visually check inside for pontoon leakage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Test for explosive gas (an indicator of vapor space leaks).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

| C.1.5.3 Fixed Roof Scaffold Support                                                            |           |          |
| Inspect scaffold support for corrosion, wear, and structural soundness.                        |           |          |
| C.1.5.4 Autogauge: Inspection Hatch and Guides (Fixed Roof)                                    |           |          |
| a) Check the hatch for corrosion and missing bolts.                                            |           |          |
| b) Look for corrosion on the tape guide’s and float guide’s wire anchors.                      |           |          |
| C.1.5.5 Autogauge: Float Well Cover                                                            |           |          |
| a) Inspect for corrosion.                                                                      |           |          |
| b) Check tape cable for wear or fraying caused by rubbing on the cover.                        |           |          |
| C.1.5.6 Sample Hatch (Internal Floating Roof)                                                  |           |          |
| a) Check overall conditions.                                                                   |           |          |
| b) When equipped with a fabric seal, check for automatic sealing after sampling.               |           |          |
| c) When equipped with a recoil reel opening device, check for proper operations.               |           |          |
| C.1.5.7 Roof-mounted Vents (Internal Floating Roof)                                            |           |          |
| Check condition of screens, locking and pivot pins.                                            |           |          |
| C.1.5.8 Gauging Platform Drip Ring                                                             |           |          |
| On fixed roof tanks with drip rings under the gauging platform or sampling area, inspect       |           |          |
| for plugged drain return to the tank.                                                          |           |          |
| C.1.5.9 Emergency Roof Drains                                                                  |           |          |
| Inspect vapor plugs for emergency drain: that seal fabric discs are slightly smaller than      |           |          |
| the pipe ID and that fabric seal is above the liquid level.                                    |           |          |
| C.1.5.10 Removable Roof Leg Racks                                                              |           |          |
| Check for leg racks on roof.                                                                   |           |          |
| C.1.5.11 Vacuum Breakers                                                                       |           |          |
| Report size, number, and type of vacuum breakers. Inspect vacuum breakers. If high legs        |           |          |
| are set, check for setting of mechanical breaker in high leg position.                         |           |          |
| C.1.5.12 Rim Vents                                                                             |           |          |
| a) Check condition of the screen on the rim vent cover.                                        |           |          |
| b) Check for plating off or removal of rim vents where jurisdictional rules do not permit      |           |          |
| removal.                                                                                       |           |          |
| C.1.5.13 Pontoon Inspection Hatches                                                            |           |          |
| a) Open pontoon inspection hatch covers and visually check inside for pontoon leakage.         |           |          |
| b) Test for explosive gas (an indicator of vapor space leaks).                                 |           |          |
<<TABLE_END>>

<<PAGE_121>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>T ANK  I NSPECTION , R EPAIR , A LTERATION ,  AND  R ECONSTRUCTION
C-9<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Tank Out-of-service Inspection Checklist (Continued)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Item
Completed<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Comments<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.1
Overview<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Check that tank has been cleaned, is gas free, and safe for entry.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Check that the tank is completely isolated from product lines, all electrical power, and
steam lines.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Check that roof is adequately supported, including fixed roof structure and floating
roof legs.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Check for presence of falling object hazards, such as corroded-through roof rafters,
asphalt stalactites, and trapped hydrocarbons in unopened or plugged equipment or
appurtenances, ledges, etc.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Inspect for slipping hazards on the bottom and roof decks.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
Inspect structural welds on accessways and clips.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) Check surfaces needing inspection for a heavy-scale buildup and check weld seams
and oily surfaces where welding is to be done. Note areas needing more cleaning,
including blasting.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h) Review cathodic protection potential readings.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.2
Tank Exterior<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect appurtenances opened during cleaning such as lower floating swing sheave
assemblies, nozzle interiors (after removal of valves).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Hammer test or ultrasonically test the roof.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Enter and inspect the floating roof pontoon compartments.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.3
Bottom Interior Surface<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Using a flashlight held close to and parallel to the bottom plates, and using the bottom
plate layout as a guide, visually inspect and hammer test the entire bottom.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Measure the depth of pitting and describe the pitting appearance (sharp edged, lake
type, dense, scattered, etc.)<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Mark areas requiring patching or further inspection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Mark locations for turning coupons for inspection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Inspect all welds for corrosion and leaks, particularly the shell-to-bottom weld.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
Inspect sketch plates for corrosion.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) Check condition of internal sump, if applicable. Standing liquid should be removed
from the sump to allow for complete inspection and vacuum testing of weld seams as
appropriate. Sump bottom and sidewall plate and seams need to be evaluated
for both product-side and soil-side corrosion.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h) Locate and mark voids under the bottom.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>i)
Record bottom data on a layout sketch using the existing bottom plates as a grid.
List the number and sizes of patches required.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>j)
Vacuum test the bottom lap welds.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>k) Hammer test or ultrasonically examine any slightly discolored spots or damp areas.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>l)
Check for reinforcing pads under all bottom attached clips, brackets, and supports.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>m) Inspect floating roof leg pads for pitting or cutting, and excessive dimpling (indicating
excessive loading).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>n) Check the column bases of fixed roof supports for adequate pads and restraining clips.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>o) In earthquake Zones 3 and 4, check that roof supports are not welded down to the
tank bottom, but are only restrained from horizontal movement.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>p) Check area beneath swing line cable for indications of cable cutting or dragging.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>q) Mark old oil and air test connection for removal and patching.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>r)
Identify and report low areas on the bottom that do not drain adequately.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>s) Inspect coating for holes, disbonding, deterioration, and discoloration.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>C-10
API S TANDARD  653<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Tank Out-of-service Inspection Checklist (Continued)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Item
Completed<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Comments<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.4
Shell Seams and Plate<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) On cone up bottoms, closely inspect and gauge the depth of metal loss on the lower
2 in. to 4 in. of the shell (area of standing water).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Measure the depth of pitting on each course.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Inspect and estimate the amount of metal loss on the heads of rivets and bolts.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Inspect shell-to-bottom riveted lap joints.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Inspect for vertical grooving damage from seal assembly protrusions.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
Inspect existing protective coatings for damage, deterioration, and disbonding.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) Check for areas of rubbing (indicating too much pressure by the seal assembly shoes
or inadequate annular space).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h) Visually inspect the shell plates and seams for indications of leakage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>i)
If the shell has riveted or bolted seams, record the leak locations by film or chart in
case the locations are lost during surface preparation for painting.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>j)
Measure annular space at 40-ft intervals.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>k) Survey the shell to check for roundness and plumb.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.5
Shell-mounted Overflows<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect overflow for corrosion and adequate screening.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Check location of overflow that it is not above any tank valves or equipment.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.6
Roof Interior Surface<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.6.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Visually inspect the underside surface of the roof plates for holes, scale buildup, and
pitting.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Hammer test or ultrasonically examine to check for thin areas, particularly in the vapor
space of floating roofs and at edge of roof on cone roof tank.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Check all clips, brackets, braces, etc., welded to the roof deck plate for welded
reinforcing pads and see that they have not broken free.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) If no pad is present, penetrant test for cracking of the weld or deck plate.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Inspect for protective coating for breaks, disbondment, and deterioration.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
Spark test the interior surface coating if recoating is not planned.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.6.2
Fixed Roof Support Structure<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect the support columns for thinning in the upper 2 ft.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) On API columns (two channels welded together) check for corrosion scale breaking
the tack welds, unless the joint between the channels is completely seal welded.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Check that the reinforcing pad on the bottom is seal-welded to the tank bottom with
horizontal movement restraining clips welded to the pad.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Determine if pipe column supports are concrete filled or open pipe. If open pipe, check
for a drain opening in the bottom of the pipe.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Inspect and gauge rafters for thinning, particularly near the center of the roof. Report
metal loss.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
Check for loose or twisted rafters.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) Inspect girders for thinning and check that they are attached securely to the top of the
columns.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>Item
Completed<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Comments<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h) Report if the columns have cross bracing in the area between the low pump out of the
top of the shell (for future internal floating roof installation).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>i)
Inspect and report presence of any roof-mounted swing line bumpers.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>j)
Photograph the roof structure if no rafter layout drawing exists.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.7
Fixed Roof Appurtenances<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.7.1
Inspection and Light Hatches<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect the hatches for corrosion, paint and coating failures, holes, and cover sealing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) On loose covers, check for a safety chain in good condition.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) On light hatches over 30 in. across, check for safety rods.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Inspect the condition of the gaskets on bold or latched down hatch covers.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.7.2
Staging Support Connection<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Inspect the condition of the staging support for corrosion.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.7.3
Breathers and Vents<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect and service the breather.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Inspect screens on vents and breathers.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.7.4
Emergency P/V Hatches<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect and service pressure/vacuum hatches. (Setting should be high enough to pre-
vent chattering of breather during normal operation. See breather manufacturer’s
guide.)<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Inspect liquid seal hatches for corrosion and proper liquid level in the seal.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.7.5
Sample Hatch<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect sample hatch for corrosion.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Check that the cover operates properly.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) If the tank has no gauge well, check for a hold-off distance marker and check mea-
surement.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.8
Floating Roof<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.8.1
Roof Deck<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Hammer test the area between roof rim and shell. (If access for hammer testing is
inadequate, measure the distance from the bottom edge of the roof to the corroded
area and then hammer test from inside the pontoon.)<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) In sour water service, clean and test all deck plate weld seams for cracking unless the
lower laps have been seal-welded.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Check that either the roof drain is open or the drain plug in the roof is open in case of
unexpected rain.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) On flat bottomed and cone bottom roof decks, check for a vapor dam around the
periphery of the roof. The dam should be continuous without break to prevent escape
of vapors to the seal area from under the center of the roof.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.8.2
Floating Roof Pontoons<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Visually inspect each pontoon for liquid leakage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Run a light wire through the gooseneck vents on locked down inspection hatch covers
to make sure they are open.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Inspect lockdown latches on each cover.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

| inadequate, measure the distance from the bottom edge of the roof to the corroded            |           |          |
| area and then hammer test from inside the pontoon.)                                          |           |          |
| b) In sour water service, clean and test all deck plate weld seams for cracking unless the   |           |          |
| lower laps have been seal-welded.                                                            |           |          |
| c) Check that either the roof drain is open or the drain plug in the roof is open in case of |           |          |
| unexpected rain.                                                                             |           |          |
| d) On flat bottomed and cone bottom roof decks, check for a vapor dam around the             |           |          |
| periphery of the roof. The dam should be continuous without break to prevent escape          |           |          |
| of vapors to the seal area from under the center of the roof.                                |           |          |
| C.2.8.2 Floating Roof Pontoons                                                               |           |          |
| a) Visually inspect each pontoon for liquid leakage.                                         |           |          |
| b) Run a light wire through the gooseneck vents on locked down inspection hatch covers       |           |          |
| to make sure they are open.                                                                  |           |          |
| c) Inspect lockdown latches on each cover.                                                   |           |          |
<<TABLE_END>>

Plate thickness ______ .<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.8.4
Floating Roof Supports<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect fixed low and removable high floating roof legs for thinning.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Inspect for notching at bottom of legs for drainage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Inspect for leg buckling or felling at bottom.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Inspect pin hole in roof guide for tears.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Check plumb of all legs.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
Inspect for adequate reinforcing gussets on all legs through a single portion of the
roof.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) Inspect the area around the roof legs for cracking if there is no internal reinforcing pad
or if the topside pad is not welded to the deck plate on the underside.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

low leg for deterioration of the gaskets.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

gauge well and/or counter-rotational device.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

of pin holes.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Inspect clips welded to roof rim for thinning.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
Seal fabric—inspect for deterioration, stiffening, holes, and tears in fabric.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) Measure length of fabric from top of shoe to roof rim, and check against maximum
anticipated annular space as roof operates.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h) Inspect any modification of shoes over shell nozzles, mixers, etc., for clearance.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>i)
Inspect shoes for damage caused by striking shell nozzles, mixers, etc.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.9.2
Primary Toroidal Assembly<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect seal fabric for wear, deterioration, holes, and tears.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>f)

tape exposed with float at lowest point.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) Check float for leakage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.11
Common Tank Appurtenances<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.11.1
Gauge Well<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect gate well pipe for thinning at about two-thirds distance above the bottom: look
for thinning at the edge of the slots.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Check for corrosion on the pipe joint. Check that sample cords, weights, thermome-
ters, etc., have been removed from the pipe.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Check for cone at bottom end of pipe about one foot above the bottom.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Check condition of well washer pipe and that its flared end is directed at the near side
of the hold off pad.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Check that supports for gauge well are welded to pad or to shell and not directly to
bottom plate.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
Check operation of gauge well cover.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) Check presence of a hold-off distance marker in well pipe and record hold-off
distance.
Hold-off distance _________ .<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h) Identify and report size and pipe schedule, and whether pipe is solid or slotted. Report
slot size.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>i)
Check that the hold-off distance plate is seal-welded to the bottom and that any gauge
well supports are welded to the plate and not directly to the bottom.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>j)
Inspect vapor control float and cable.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>k) Check for presence and condition of gauge well washer.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>l)
Check for bull plug or plate blind on gauge well washer valve.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>m) Inspect gauge well guide in floating roof for pitting and thinning.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>n) Inspect the guide rollers and sliding plates for freedom of movement.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>o) Inspect condition of gauge well pipe seal system.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>p) On black oil and diesel services: if gauge well is also used for sampling, check for
presence of a thief- and gauge-type hatch to avoid spillage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>q) Visually inspect inside of pipe for pipe weld protrusions which could catch or damage
vapor control float.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.11.2
Sampling Systems: Roof Sample Hatches<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect roof-mounted sample hatches for reinforcing pads and cracking.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Inspect cover for operation.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) For tanks complying with Air Quality Monitoring District rules, inspect sample hatch
covers for adequate sealing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Check horizontal alignment of internal floating roof sample hatches under fixed roof
hatches.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Inspect the sealing system on the internal floating roof sample hatch cover.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
Inspect floating roof sample hatch cover recoil reel and rope.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.11.3
Shell Nozzles<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect shell nozzles for thinning and pitting.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Inspect hot tap nozzles for trimming of holes.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>Item
Completed<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Comments<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Identify type of shell nozzles.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Identify and describe internal piping, including elbow-up and elbow-down types.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.11.4
For Nozzles Extended Into the Tank<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect pipe support pads welded to tank bottom.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Inspect to see that pipe is free to move along support without strain or tearing action
on bottom plate.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Inspect nozzle valves for packing leaks and damaged flange faces.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Inspect heater stream nozzle flanges and valves for wire cutting.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Report which nozzles have thermal pressure relief bosses and valves.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
In internal elbow-down fill line nozzles, inspect the wear plate on the tank bottom.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) On elbow-up fill lines in floating roof tanks, check that opening is directed against
underside of roof, not against vapor space. Inspect impact are for erosion.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.11.5
Diffusers and Air Rolling Systems<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect diffuser pipe for erosion and thinning.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Check holes in diffuser for excessive wear and enlargement.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Inspect diffuser supports for damage and corrosion.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Check that diffuser supports restrain, not anchor, longitudinal line movement.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Inspect air spiders on bottom of lube oil tanks for plugging and damaged or broken
threaded joints.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.11.6
Swing Lines<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect flexible joint for cracks and leaks.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Scribe the flexible joint across the two moving faces and raise end of swing line to
check the joint’s freedom of movement, indicated by separation of scribe marks.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Check that flexible joints over 6 in. are supported.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Inspect the swing pipe for deep pitting and weld corrosion.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Loosen the vent plugs in the pontoons and listen for a vacuum. Lack of a vacuum
indicates a leaking pontoon.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
Check the results of air test on pontoons during repairs.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) Inspect the pontoons for pitting.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h) Inspect the pull-down cable connections to the swing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>i)
Inspect the condition of the bottom-mounted support, fixed roof limiting bumper, or
shell-mounted limiting bumper for wood condition, weld and bolt corrosion, and seal
welding to bottom or shell.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>j)
Inspect safety hold-down chain for corrosion and weak links.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>k) Check that there is a welded reinforcing pad where the chain connects to the bottom.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>l)
If the floating swing in a floating or internal floating roof tank does not have a limiting
device preventing the swing from exceeding 60 degrees, measure and calculate the
maximum angle possible with the roof on overflow.
Max. angle on overflow _____________ .
(If the calculated angle exceeds 65 degrees, recommended installation of a limiting
bracket.)<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>m) Inspect pull-down cable for fraying.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.11.7
Manway Heater Racks<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect the manway heater racks for broken welds and bending of the sliding rails.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Measure and record the length of the heater and length of the track.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.11.8
Mixer Wear Plates and Deflector Stands<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect bottom and shell plates and deflector stands.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Inspect for erosion and corrosion on the wear plates. Inspect for rigidity, structural
soundness, corrosion, and erosion of deck plates and reinforcing pads that are seal-
welded to the bottom under the deflector stand legs.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Measure for propeller clearance between the bottom of deflector stand and roof when
the roof is on low legs.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.12
Access Structures<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.12.1
Handrails<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Identify and report type (steel pipe, galvanized pipe, square tube, angle) and size of
handrails.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Inspect for pitting and holes, paint failure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Inspect attachment welds.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Identify cold joints and sharp edges. Inspect the handrails and midrails.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Inspect safety drop bar (or safety chain) for corrosion, functioning, and length.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
Inspect the handrail between the rolling ladder and the gaging platform for a hazard-
ous opening when the floating roof is at its lowest level.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.12.2
Platform Frame<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect frame for corrosion and paint failure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Inspect the attachment of frame to supports and supports to tank for corrosion and
weld failure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Check reinforcing pads where supports are attached to shell or roof.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Inspect the surface that deck plate or grating rests on, for thinning and holes.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Check that flat-surface-to-flat-surface junctures are seal-welded.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.12.3
Deck Plate and Grating<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Inspect deck plate for corrosion-caused thinning or holes (not drain holes) and paint
failure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Inspect plate-to-frame weld for rust scale buildup.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Inspect grating for corrosion-caused thinning of bars and failure of welds.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=2>>Annex D
(normative)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=2>>Authorized Inspector Certification<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>D.1 Examination<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A written examination to certify an authorized inspector within the scope of API 653 shall be administered by a third party
designated by API. The examination shall be based on the current API 653 body of knowledge as published by API.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>D.2 Certification<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>D.2.1  An API 653 authorized inspector certificate will be issued when an applicant has successfully passed the API
653 certification examination, and satisfies the criteria for education and experience. Education and experience, when
combined, shall be equal to at least one of the following.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) A bachelor of science degree in engineering or technology plus one year of experience in supervision or
performance of inspection activities as described in API 653.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) A two-year degree or certificate in engineering or technology, plus two years of experience in the design,
construction, repair, inspection, or operation of aboveground storage tanks, of which one year must be in
supervision or performance of inspection activities as described in API 653.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) A high school diploma or equivalent, plus three years of experience in the design, construction, repair, inspection,
or operation of aboveground storage tanks, of which one year must be in supervision or performance of inspection
activities as described in API 653.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) A minimum of five years of experience in the design, construction, repair, inspection, or operation of aboveground
storage tanks, of which one year must be in supervision or performance of inspection activities as described in
API 653.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>D.2.2  An API certificate for an authorized inspector is valid for three years from its date of issuance.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>D.2.3  An API 653 authorized inspector certificate is valid in all jurisdictions and any other location that accepts or
other wise does not prohibit the use of API 653.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>D.3 Certification Agency<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>API shall be the certifying agency.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>D.4 Retroactivity<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The certification requirements of API 653 shall not be retroactive or interpreted as applying before 12 months after
the date of publication of this edition or addendum of API 653. The recertification requirements of D.5 shall not be
retroactive or interpreted as applying before three years after the date of publication of this edition or addendum of
API 653.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>D.5 Recertification<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>D.5.1  Recertification is required three years from the date of issuance of the API 653 authorized inspector
certificate. Recertification by written examination will be required for authorized inspectors who have not been actively
engaged as authorized inspectors within the most recent three-year certification period. Recertification exams will be
in accordance with all of the provisions contained in API 653.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>D-1<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_132>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>D-2
API S TANDARD  653<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>D.5.2  Actively engaged as an authorized inspector shall be defined as one of the following provisions:<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) a minimum of 20 % of the time spent performing inspection activities, or supervision of inspection activities, or
engineering support of inspection activities as described in API 653 over the most recent three-year certification
period;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) performance of inspection activities or supervision of inspection activities or engineering support of inspection
activities on 75 aboveground storage tanks as described in API 653 over the most recent three-year certification
period<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE   Inspection activities common to other API inspection documents (NDE, record keeping, review of welding documents,
etc.) may be considered here.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>D.5.3  Once every other recertification period (every six years), inspectors actively engaged as an authorized inspector
shall demonstrate knowledge of revisions to API 653 that were instituted during the previous six years. This requirement
shall be effective six years from the inspector’s initial certification date.  Inspectors who have not been actively engaged
as an authorized inspector within the most recent three-year period shall recertify as required in D.5.1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PAGE_139>>
<<HEADING level=2>>Annex G
(informative)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=2>>Qualification of Tank Bottom Examination Procedures and Personnel<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.1 Introduction<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.1.1  This annex provides guidance for qualifying both tank bottom examination procedures and individuals that
perform tank bottom examinations. Owner/operators may elect to either apply this annex as written or modify it to meet
their own applications and needs. Tank bottom examinations are an important factor in providing the owner/operator
increased assurance of tank integrity. As a result, it is important that qualified examination procedures and personnel
are used in these examinations. Specific agreements and requirements for qualification of tank bottom examination
procedures and tank bottom examiners should be established between the owner/operator and the authorized
inspection agency.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.1.2  There have been many NDE tools developed for examining tank bottoms. Most of these tools are complex
and require the operator to have a high level of knowledge and skill. The effectiveness of these examinations may
vary greatly depending on the equipment used, the examination procedure, and the skill of the examiner.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Often the owner/operator will not have the ability to easily determine if the tank bottom examination has been effective
in assessing the actual condition of the tank bottom. The requirements in this annex will provide the owner/operator
additional assurance that the tank bottom examination will find significant metal loss.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.2 Definitions<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.2.1
authorized inspection agency
Organizations that employ an aboveground storage tank inspector certified by API (see 3.3).<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.2.2
bottom scan
The use of equipment over large portions of the tank bottom to detect corrosion in a tank bottom. One common type
of bottom-scanning equipment is the magnetic flux leakage (MFL) scanner.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.2.3
essential variables
Variables in the procedure that cannot be changed without the procedure and scanning operators being re-qualified.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.2.4
examiners
Scanning operators and NDE technicians who prove-up bottom indications.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.2.5
non-essential variables
Variables in the procedure that can be changed without having to re-qualify the procedure and/or scanning operators.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.2.6
qualification test
The demonstration test that is used to prove that a procedure or examiner can successfully find and prove-up tank
bottom metal loss.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G-1<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_140>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G-2
API S TANDARD  653<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.2.7
scanning operator
operator
The individual that operates bottom-scanning equipment.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.2.8
sizing
prove-up
The activity that is used to accurately determine the remaining bottom thickness in areas where indications are found
by the bottom scanning equipment. This is often accomplished using the UT method.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.2.9
tank bottom examination
The examination of a tank bottom using special equipment to determine the remaining thickness of the tank bottom. It
includes both the detection and prove-up of the indications. It does not include the visual examination that is included
in the internal inspection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.2.10
tank bottom examination procedure
TBP
A qualified written procedure that addresses the essential and non-essential variables for the tank bottom
examination. The procedure can include multiple methods and tools, i.e. bottom scanner, hand scanner, and UT
prove-up.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.2.11
tank bottom examiner qualification record
TBEQ
A record of the qualification test for a specific scanning operator. This record must contain the data for all essential
variables and the results of the qualification test.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.2.12
tank bottom procedure qualification record
TBPQ
A record of the qualification test for a tank bottom examination procedure. This record must contain the data for all
essential variables and the results of the qualification test.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.2.13
variables or procedure variables
The specific data in a procedure that provides direction and limitations to the scanning operator. Examples include:
plate thickness, overlap of adjacent bottom scans, scanning speed, equipment settings, etc.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.3 Tank Bottom Examination Procedures<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.3.1  Each authorized inspection agency performing tank bottom examinations is responsible to have and use
TBPs. These procedures provide direction for examiners performing tank bottom examinations. A procedure also
allows the owner/operator or authorized inspector to verify whether the examiners are correctly performing the
examinations.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.3.2  The authorized inspection agency that performs the tank bottom examinations should develop the TBPs.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.3.3  Each TBP shall address essential and non-essential variables. Section G.5.3 provides guidance for
determining appropriate TBP essential and non-essential variables. Each procedure should specify limits on
appropriate variables, e.g. plate thickness range.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_141>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>T ANK  I NSPECTION , R EPAIR , A LTERATION ,  AND  R ECONSTRUCTION
G-3<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.4 Tank Bottom Examiners<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.4.1  Examiners need only to be qualified for the work they do in the field. For example, scanning operators who
only use the bottom scanning equipment and do not prove-up the flaw with a follow-up method need only to be
qualified for the scanning operation.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.4.2  The purpose of qualifying the tank bottom examiner is to determine if the examiner is capable of satisfactorily
using a qualified procedure to determine the condition of the tank bottom.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.4.3  Each authorized inspection agency is responsible to train, test and qualify the scanning operators and
examiners they employ using follow-up techniques. Qualifications gained through one authorized inspection agency
are not necessarily valid for any other authorized inspection agency [see G.4.4 and G.4.9 f)].<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.4.4  The authorized inspection agency is responsible for training each scanning operator they employ. Each
scanning operator should receive a minimum of 40 hours of training. This training should include:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) instruction on the NDE principles/methods used by the bottom scanner, limitations and application of the specific
scanning equipment and procedure, scanning equipment calibration and operation, key scanning equipment
operating variables, etc.;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) hands-on operation of the bottom scanner under the direct supervision of a qualified scanning examiner.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>When hiring experienced examiners, the authorized inspection agency should verify and document previous
examiner training and provide any additional training if necessary. Experienced examiners should be provided
training regarding specific procedural requirements and test equipment to be utilized by the new employer.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.4.5  The authorized inspection agency is responsible for testing each scanning operator by written examination.
The test questions should be appropriate for the scanning method to be used. The authorized inspection agency
should establish the passing score for the written examination.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.4.6  The authorized inspection agency is responsible for qualifying all examiners they employ. All examiners
(scanning operators and examiners performing prove-up on the indications) shall be qualified by performing an
examination on test plates as specified in G.5. Only third-party companies, having no conflict of interest in tank bottom
examination applications, or owner/operator companies may facilitate qualification tests. The examiner shall be
considered qualified if the acceptance criteria specified in G.5.3 has been met.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Examiners performing prove-up of indications using ultrasonic testing methods should be qualified in accordance
with API 650, Section 8.3.2 and supplemental requirements given in this annex.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.4.7  During the qualification test, a TBEQ must be completed for each examiner. The TBEQ is a record of the
variables used during the qualification test. On the TBEQ, the qualifying company must record:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) the essential variables from the qualification test;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) the qualification test results;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) number of hours the individual has been trained;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) test score from the written training examination.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The TBEQ shall be certified (signed) as accurate by a representative of the authorized inspection agency and a
representative of the company facilitating the test.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.4.8  The TBEQ may be written in any format that contains all the required information.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_142>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G-4
API S TANDARD  653<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.4.9  The bottom-scanning examiners (operators and/or UT examiners) should be re-qualified when any of the
following apply:<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) when the examiner is not qualified to the TBP that is to be used at the owner/operator facility;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) when the authorized inspection agency changes the TBP and that change requires the procedure to be re-
qualified;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) when the operator has not performed a tank bottom scan in six months;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) when the operator has not used the specific procedure (TBP) for 12 months;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) when the authorized inspection agency has reason to question the ability of the examiner;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f) when an examiner changes to a new employing authorized inspection agency that uses procedures with essential
variables that are different from the previous employer’s procedures.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.5 Qualification Testing<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.5.1 Qualification Test Plates<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.5.1.1  The qualification test will be performed on a sample tank bottom with designed flaws. The sample tank bottom
should be a minimum of 70 ft 2  to provide space for the designed flaws. The plate material used to fabricate sample
plates may be either new steel or used steel. It should be noted that the results obtained during qualification tests might
not be indicative of the results of examinations performed on other plates of differing quality or permeability. When used
steel is utilized for qualification purposes, the qualification test acceptance standards recommended in G.5.2 may not be
appropriate. The owner/operator should establish its own acceptance standards in such cases.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.5.1.2  The minimum number and types of underside test pits located on the test plates are described below:<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Remaining Bottom

<<HEADING level=3>>G.5.3 Qualification Test Variables<<HEADING_END>>

additional variables should be considered essential variables for each tank bottom scanner.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.5.3.3  Essential variables and the values must be recorded on the TBP and on the TBEQ.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>G.5.3.4  Non-essential variables are those items that will have a lesser effect on the quality of the examination. Non-
essential variables may be different for different types of tank bottom scanners.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
