<<HEADING level=2>>Annex H
(informative)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=2>>Similar Service Assessment<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This annex is provided as guidance for performing a similar service assessment. This annex is not all inclusive and is
not mandatory. It is not intended to prevent the use of other similar service assessment methods. This annex contains
sample datasheets illustrating items that should be considered when conducting a similar service assessment. The
datasheet format facilitates the recording of assessment findings.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1  The following examples are merely examples for illustration purposes only. Each company should develop its own
approach. They are not to be considered exclusive or exhaustive in nature. API makes no warranties, express or implied for
reliance on or any omissions from the information contained in this document.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2  Where applicable, authorities having jurisdiction should be consulted.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>H-1<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_148>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>H-2
API S TANDARD  653<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>H.1 Scope<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This annex provides guidance for conducting a similar service assessment to establish inspection intervals for tanks
for which corrosion rates have not been directly measured as referenced in 6.3.2 and 6.4.2. This annex is intended for
use by an authorized inspector, storage tank engineer and other person(s) having knowledge and experience in
performing similar service assessments.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>H.2 Similar Service Assessment<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Several criteria must be evaluated to determine whether the candidate tank is in similar service with the control tank.
Similar service assessment requires a sufficient amount of data collection and analysis and needs to be performed in a
comprehensive and thorough fashion in accordance with an established risk management program. Similar service
assessment is conducted using design, construction, operation, maintenance and inspection data. Data should be
obtained by using direct and indirect examination procedures such as MT and UT, evaluating product corrosivity,
measuring CP levels, determining soil properties, and other factors. Refer to the “Similar Service Assessment—
Datasheet,” which provides a place to record the required data. Data should be collected for each of the tank
characteristics listed on the datasheet for both the control tank and candidate tanks and an assessment made to
determine if the services are similar. Typically, there will not be an exact match of all data, or some of the required data
will not even be known. When there is not an exact match between one or more criteria, additional evaluation is
necessary to determine whether the tanks can be considered to be in similar service. Figure H.1 illustrates the steps in
conducting a similar service assessment. The “Similar Service Assessment—Datasheet” is to facilitate the comparison
of data for the two tanks. If the criteria for the control tank and candidate tank match, the candidate tank may be
considered in similar service as the control tank for that particular criterion.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>H.2.1 Additional Assessment<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>When additional assessment is required because an individual basic criterion does not match, the table references
the section describing additional factors that must be assessed. If the additional factors in the specified reference
section are assessed to be sufficiently similar, the tanks are considered in similar service for that factor. If all additional
provisions are satisfied, the tanks are considered in similar service. Additional assessment(s) must be documented
and maintained in the record file as per 6.8.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>H.2.1.1   Year Tank Erected :   If the criteria for the control tank and candidate tank do not match, the following
additional provisions must be satisfied to consider both tanks in similar service:<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) the difference in ages of the tanks must be considered in the corrosion rate calculations, and<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) any substantive differences in the design and/or construction standards to which the tanks were constructed must
be considered in the similar service evaluation.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>H.2.1.2    Bottom Material : If the criteria for the control tank and candidate tank do not match, the following additional
provisions must be satisfied to consider both tanks in similar service:<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) the bottom material of the candidate tank must have similar corrosion-resistance properties as the bottom material
of the control tank,<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) the candidate tank, or both the candidate and the control tanks, utilize an effective lining to prevent corrosion of the
product-side of the bottom, and<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) the potential for corrosion of the soil-side of the bottom is assessed to be similar for both tank bottom materials.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_149>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>T ANK  I NSPECTION , R EPAIR , A LTERATION ,  AND  R ECONSTRUCTION
H-3<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>H.2.1.3  Shell Material :   If the criteria for the control tank and candidate tank do not match, the following additional
provisions must be satisfied to consider both tanks in similar service:<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) the shell material of the candidate tank must have similar corrosion-resistance properties as the shell material of
the control tank,<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) the candidate tank, or both the candidate and the control tanks, utilize a suitable lining to prevent corrosion of the
product-side of the shell, and<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) the candidate tank, or both the candidate and the control tanks, utilize a suitable paint or coating to prevent
corrosion of the external side of the shell.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>H.2.1.4  Corrosion Allowance, Bottom/Shell : If the criteria for the control tank and candidate tank do not match, the
difference in corrosion allowance should be accounted for in the remaining life and inspection interval calculations to
consider both tanks in similar service.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>H.2.1.5  Bottom Lining Type/Thickness/Age :   If the criteria for the control tank and candidate tank do not match, the
differences in the bottom lining systems must be assessed. The provisions of API 652 should be used to assess the
relative corrosion protection provided by the different lining systems.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>H.2.1.6  Cathodic Protection : If the criteria for the control tank and candidate tank do not match, the following
additional provisions shall apply. The provisions of API 651 should be used to assess the relative corrosion protection
provided by the cathodic protection systems:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) if the candidate tank is protected with a properly designed and functional cathodic protection system, and the
control tank is not, the candidate tank may be considered to be in similar service with respect to cathodic
protection;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) if the control tank is protected with a properly designed and functional cathodic protection system, and the
candidate tank is not, the candidate tank may not be considered to be in similar service with respect to cathodic
protection;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) if the control tank and the candidate tank are protected with properly designed and functional cathodic protection
systems, the tanks may be considered to be in similar service with respect to cathodic protection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>H.2.1.7  Double Bottom :   If the candidate tank and/or the control tank has multiple bottoms, the similar service
assessment of soil-side corrosion should be based on the material that is in contact with the underside of the primary
(upper) bottom plate<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>H.2.1.8  Soil/Material in Contact with Bottom Plate :   Any differences in the following factors between the control and
the candidate tank must be assessed in determining whether the candidate tank is in similar service as the control
tank:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) soil or material type;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) pH;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) alkalinity;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) moisture;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) salinity;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f) resistivity;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_150>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>H-4
API S TANDARD  653<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) oil type (if oiled sand foundation);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h) soil/material cleanliness;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>i) soil gradation;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>j) chlorides;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>k) sulfates.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>H.2.1.9  Ambient Conditions :   Any differences in the following factors between the control tank and the candidate
tank must be assessed in determining whether the candidate tank is in similar service as the control tank:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) low one day mean temperature;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) exposure to salt air or other corrosive elements.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>H.2.1.10    Current Service Conditions :   Any differences in the following factors between the control tank and the
candidate tank must be assessed in determining whether the candidate tank is in similar service as the control tank:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) product classification (see Table H.1);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) specific gravity of liquid;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Reid vapor pressure at 60  ° F;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) normal operating temperature;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) inert gas blanket, if used;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f) water bottom, if used;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) sulfur content;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h) length of time in service;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>i) product corrosivity.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>H.2.1.11  Previous Service Conditions : If the control tank and/or candidate tank have previously been used for
different services than the current service, the same factors described in H.2.1.10 should be evaluated for the
previous service conditions.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>H.2.1.12   Product Classification : Table H.1 classifies a wide variety of liquids commonly stored in aboveground
storage tanks. This table serves as guidance in assessing current or previous service conditions.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>H.2.1.13  Additional Considerations :   In addition to the factors discussed above, the following data, if available for the
control tank and the candidate tank, should be assessed in determining whether the candidate tank is in similar
service as the control tank:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) MFL data for the tank bottom;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) ultrasonic thickness (UT) measurement data;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) fiber optic monitoring system data;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_151>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>T ANK  I NSPECTION , R EPAIR , A LTERATION ,  AND  R ECONSTRUCTION
H-5<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) cathodic protection monitoring tube data;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) tank bottom integrity testing data;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f) maintenance procedures, including frequency and methods of tank cleaning.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>H.3 Example of Remaining Life Determination<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>H.3.1 Tank Bottom<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Figure H.2 illustrates one method of determining the time interval in which a tank bottom will reach its minimum
bottom plate thickness, beyond which the tank should be repaired or removed from service. In this example, the
original metal thickness was  1 / 4  in. when the tank was constructed in 1970. The minimum bottom plate thickness at
the next inspection interval was 0.05 in. (See also Table 4.4.) At the time of this evaluation (June 10, 1990), the tank
was in sour crude service. Previous service included 20 years in sour crude service. Based on thicknesses measured
and the calculated corrosion rate, the remaining life, or time to reach the minimum bottom plate thickness of 0.050 in.
is projected to be approximately 20 years, or June 10, 2010. See 4.4.5 for the minimum thickness calculation for a
tank bottom.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>H.3.2 Tank Shell<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Figure H.3 illustrates one method of determining the time interval in which a tank shell course will reach its limit of
metal loss, beyond which the tank should be repaired or removed from service. In this example, the original metal
thickness was  1 / 2  in. when the tank was constructed in 1990. The limit of metal loss of the top shell course was
calculated to be  1 / 4  in. At the time of this evaluation (November 15, 2002), the tank was in sweet gasoline service.
Previous services included nearly seven years in sweet crude and nearly three years in sour crude service. Based
on thicknesses measured at periodic inspections and corrosion rates calculated from them, the remaining life, or
time to reach the metal loss limit of  1 / 4  in. is projected to be approximately four years, or August 1, 2006. See 4.3.3
for the minimum thickness calculation for an entire shell course.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=2>>Annex I
(informative)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=2>>Inquiries and Suggestions for Change<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.1 Introduction<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This annex describes the process established by API for 1) submitting inquiries to API, and 2) for submitting
suggestions for changes to this standard. Inquiries and suggestions for change are welcome and encouraged
because they provide useful reader feedback to the responsible API Committee regarding technical accuracy, current
technology use, clarity, consistency, and completeness of the standard. API will attempt to answer all valid inquiries.
Submittals not complying with this Annex will be returned unanswered.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Sections I.2 through I.7, below, cover the submitting of inquiries. See Section I.8 for instructions about submitting
suggestions for change.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.2 Inquiry References<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.2.1  API maintains several websites that provide information that should be considered when considering
submitting an inquiry.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.2.2  Your inquiry may have been previously formally addressed by the Subcommittee and the resulting
interpretation posted on the API website as follows:<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>— For all standards: http://mycommittees.api.org/standards/techinterp/default.aspx<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>— For Refining Standards: http://mycommittees.api.org/standards/techinterp/refequip/default.aspx<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For both links, click on the standard in question to download the file.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.2.3  In addition, an addendum or errata, which may have addressed your issue, can be found on the API website
as follows:<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>— For all standards: http://www.api.org/standards/addenda/<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>— For Refining Standards: http://www.api.org/standards/addenda/add-ref.cfm<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.3 Definitions<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>I.3.1  Inquiry: A question that asks what is the meaning of a specific paragraph, figure, or table in the standard; i.e.
what do the words say. It is not a question that asks about the intention of the standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.3.2  The answer to the inquiry. Typically, the answer is simply a “Yes” or “No” response, with a brief clarification if
needed. This term is also used to refer to the combined question and answer.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.4 API Policy Regarding Inquiries<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.4.1  API has established the following limits on its activity in the handling of inquiries.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) API does not approve, certify, rate, or endorse any item, construction, proprietary device, or activity.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) API does not act as a consultant on specific engineering problems.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>I-1<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_162>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>I-2
API S TANDARD  653<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) API does not provide information on the general understanding or application of the standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.4.2  All inquiries that result in interpretations will be made available to the public on the API website.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.5 Submission of Inquiries<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.5.1  An electronic form for submitting a request can be found on the API Web site at http://rfi.api.org/. Please use
this means to submit your inquiry.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.5.2  All inquiries must comply with the following.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Current standard: If an inquiry refers to a version or addendum that is not the latest, the Subcommittee will develop
the interpretation based on the requirements stated in the current version.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Specific Reference: The applicable paragraph number, figure number, or table number must be cited in the inquiry.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Sentence Structure: Inquiries must be written such that the answer can be a YES or NO, with technical details
added if necessary. The inquiry statement should be technically and editorially correct, and written in
understandable English.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) Background: Providing a background explanation is optional, but is encouraged to assist the committee in
understanding the query.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) Single Subject: The scope of an inquiry shall be limited to a single subject or a group of closely related subjects.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f) General Format:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1) The general format of the inquiry should be as follows: “Does Paragraph XXX of API-6XX require that ….?”<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>2) The inquirer shall state what is required in his or her option, as the answer to the query.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>3) If a revision to the standard is believed to also be needed, provide recommended wording.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) The Inquirer should not use the inquiry process to improve his general understanding, design skills, and usage of
the standard. Consultants not affiliated with API are available for this purpose.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h) It is important that the Inquirer understand the difference between an inquiry and a suggestion for change. API
encourages both, but the submittal and committee handling procedures are different.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.5.3  General guidelines for submission can also be found on the API web site at:<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>http://www.api.org/Publications-Standards-and-Statistics/FAQs-and-Inquiries/FAQs/Technical-Question/
Guidelines-for-submission.aspx<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.6 Typical Inquiry Procedure<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.6.1  The typical procedure of an inquiry is as follows.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) The Inquirer must prepare the inquiry, including any necessary background information, in full compliance with this
Annex and submit to the API Standards Coordinator.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) API Standards Coordinator checks the inquiry to verify compliance with the requirements of submitting an inquiry.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_163>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>T ANK  I NSPECTION , R EPAIR , A LTERATION ,  AND  R ECONSTRUCTION
I-3<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) If the inquiry cannot be answered for any reason, the Coordinator will issue a response to the inquirer advising the
reason(s) for not answering the inquiry. A form or checklist will typically be used for this response.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) If the Coordinator believes inquiry is valid, it will be forwarded to the Subcommittee for study, and the inquirer will
be advised using the form letter.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) The Subcommittee will evaluate the inquiry and either develop a response or determine that the inquiry cannot be
answered, and advise the Coordinator accordingly. The Subcommittee will consider the need for modifying the
standard to resolve technical issues, add new requirements, make editorial corrections, improve clarity, remove
conflicts, etcetera.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f) The interpretation will be published on the API website when approved by the Subcommittee.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.6.2  The time required to process a valid inquiry as described in I.6.1 may take as long as a year.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.7 Interpretations Responding to Inquiries<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>I.7.1  An interpretation is written by the Subcommittee to provide the specific answer to an inquiry. It typically will not
state the intent of the standard, nor give reasons for the requirements, nor give historical bases, nor provide overall
understanding of the standard. If the inquiry is properly phrased, the interpretation can be a one-word response. With
many inquiries, there may be a need to provide clarifying statements, such as the limits on the applicability.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>I.7.2  Although it is not possible to develop interpretations quickly to remedy immediate needs, the industry benefits
as a whole when inquiries are utilized as a means of trying to understand the technical requirements in the standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.8 Suggestions for Changes<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.8.1  “Suggestion for Change” is not an inquiry; it is simply a communication (email preferred) from a reader to API
proposing that a specific change be made to the standard.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.8.2  Any format is acceptable, as long as the content is clear.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>I.8.3  The most effective means to submit suggestions is to send an email to the API Coordinator
(standards@api.org).<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>I.8.4  The content of a suggestion must include the standard number, edition, and addendum in question. The
relevant paragraph numbers, table number, figure number, etc. must also be stated. Provide as much explanation as
necessary to be sure the Subcommittee understands the technical issues. Provide specific language that you think is
needed to implement the change. Last, include your name, company affiliation if any, and your return email or mailing
address.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>I.8.5  API will forward all suggestions that are suitably written to the Subcommittee for consideration. The
Subcommittee will evaluate each suggestion and determine if a change is needed. Suggestions that are accepted by
the Subcommittee will be reflected in a future edition or addenda, but a reply advising the submitter of the
Subcommittee's decision may not be issued.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_164>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_165>>
<<HEADING level=2>>Annex S
(normative)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=2>>Austenitic Stainless Steel Storage Tanks<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.1 Scope<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.1.1  This annex covers the inspection, repair, alteration, and reconstruction of stainless steel tanks that were
constructed in accordance with API 650, Annex S.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.1.2  This annex states only the requirements that differ from the basic rules in this standard. For requirements not
stated, the basic rules must be followed.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.2 References<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>No changes to Section 2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.3 Definitions<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>No changes to Section 3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.4 Suitability for Service<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.4.1  In 4.2.4.1, the requirements of API 650, Section S.3.5 shall also be satisfied.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.4.2  In 4.2.4.3, Annex M requirements shall be met for stainless steel tanks with design temperatures over 40  ° C
(100  ° F) as modified by API 650, Sections S.3.6.2 thru S.3.6.7.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>S.4.3  In 4.3.3.1, the maximum allowable stress  S  shall be modified as follows, for the design condition ( S d ) and the
hydrostatic test condition ( S t ) the maximum allowable stress for all shell courses shall be the lesser of 0.95 Y  or 0.4 T .<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.4.4  Table 4.2 shall be in accordance with API 650, Table S-4. When the radiography schedule applied to the
existing weld is unknown, the joint efficiency of 0.7 shall be used.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.4.5  Section 4.3.3.5 c), shall be changed to read “Operation at temperatures over 40  ° C (100  ° F).”<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.4.6  In 4.3.3.6, the factor  2 / 3 Y  shall be replaced with  3 / 4 Y .<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.4.7  In 4.3.4, these rules do not cover stainless steel tanks.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.5 Brittle Fracture<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The tank is suitable for continued use in ambient temperature service.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.6 Inspection<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>No changes to Section 6.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.7 Materials<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.7.1  In 7.3.1.2, add reference to ASTM A480.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.7.2  Structural may be shapes fabricated from plate. Plate and structural material shall meet API 650, Section S.2.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>S-1<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>S-2
API S TANDARD  653<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.8 Design Considerations for Reconstructed Tanks<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In 8.4.3, the allowable stress shall be revised to meet the allowable stresses of API 650, Section S.3.2.2.1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.9 Tank Repair and Alteration<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.9.1  In applying 9.1.1 to fabrication and construction requirements, API 650, Sections S.4.1 through S.4.9 shall be
met as applicable.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.9.2  Hot taps for stainless steels (reference Section 9.14) are not addressed by this annex.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.10 Dismantling and Reconstruction<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.10.1  In 10.4.2, welding shall also meet the requirements of API 650, Section S.4.11.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.10.2  Thermal cutting of stainless steel shall be by the iron powder burning, carbon arc, plasma-arc, water jet, or
laser cutting methods.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.10.3  The storage requirements of API 650, Section S.4.2 shall be met.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.10.4  If specified by the owner/operator, the requirements of API 650, Section S.4.5 shall be met.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.11 Welding<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Welding shall also meet the requirements of API 650, Sections S.4.11 and S.4.12.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.12 Examination and Testing<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.12.1  Any reference to magnetic particle method shall be replaced with the liquid penetrant method.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.12.2  In 12.3, the quality of test water shall meet API 650, Section S.4.10.2.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>S.13 Annexes<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Annex F (NDE Requirements Summary)—any references to magnetic particle examination shall be disregarded.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=2>>Annex SC
(normative)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=2>>Stainless and Carbon Steel Mixed Storage Tanks<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.1 Scope<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.1.1  This annex covers the inspection, repair, alteration and reconstruction of mixed material tanks constructed in
accordance with API 650, Annex SC.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>SC.1.2  This annex states only the requirements that differ from the basic rules in this standard, Annex S of this
standard, Annex X of this standard and API 650, Annex SC. For requirements not stated, the basic rules shall be
followed.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.1.3  In this annex the term “stainless steel” includes austenitic or duplex stainless steel unless noted otherwise.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.2 References<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>No changes to Section 2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.3 Definitions<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>No changes to Section 3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.4 Suitability for Service<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.4.1  Revise to 4.2.4.1: The requirements of API 650, Sections S.3.5 and API 650, and X.3.6, shall also be
satisfied for the stainless steel components of the tank.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>SC.4.2  Revise 4.2.4.3: This annex applies to tanks in non-refrigerated services with a maximum design temperature
not exceeding 260 °C (500 °F). For the purposes of this annex, the design temperature shall be the maximum design
temperature as specified by the owner/operator.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE   Exothermic reactions occurring inside unheated storage tanks can produce temperatures exceeding 40 °C (100 °F).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>SC.4.3  Add to 4.3.3.1: The maximum allowable stress  S  shall be modified as follows, for the design condition ( Sd )
and the hydrotest condition ( St ) the maximum allowable stress for austenitic stainless steel shell courses shall be the
smaller of 0.95 Y  or 0.4 T .<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>SC.4.4  Table 4-2—Joint efficiencies for welded joints shall be in accordance with API 650, Table S-4, or API 650,
Table X-3. When the radiography schedule applied to the existing weld is unknown, then the joint efficiency of 0.7
shall be used.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.4.5  Revise 4.3.3.5.c to read ‘Operation at temperatures over 40 °C (100 °F).’<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.4.6  Revise 4.3.3.6 by replacing the  2 / 3 Y  factor with  3 / 4 Y  for austenitic stainless steel components.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.4.7  The rules in 4.3.4 for riveted tanks do not cover mixed material tanks.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.5 Brittle Fracture Considerations<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Evaluation of brittle fracture shall be done according to Section 5 of this standard for carbon steel, Section S.5 of this
standard for austenitic stainless steel, and Section X.5 of this standard for duplex stainless steel components.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>SC-1<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>SC-2
API S TANDARD  653<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.6 Inspection<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>No Changes to Section 6.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.7 Materials<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Materials requirements for mixed materials situations are unchanged from the base document except as modified by
API 653 Appendices S and X (S.7 and X.7) for stainless steels.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.8 Design Considerations for Reconstructed Tanks<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The allowable stress in 8.4.2 and 8.4.3 for stainless steel components shall be revised to meet the allowable stresses
of API 650 Annex S or API 650 Annex X.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.9 Tank Repair and Alteration<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.9.1  Revise 9.2 to read: Shell insert plates shall be made in accordance with API 650, Annex SC 3.2.2.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.9.2  Revise 9.3 to read: Lap patches shall be made carbon steel to carbon steel and stainless steel to stainless
steel<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.9.3  Revise 9.8 to read: Shell penetrations and reinforcing shall be made in accordance with API 650, Annex SC
3.4.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.9.4  Revise 9.10 to read: Repair of tank bottoms shall be made in accordance with API 650, Annex SC 3.1.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.9.5  Revise 9.14 to read: Hot taps in stainless steel are not addressed by this annex.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC.10 Other<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For Dismantling and Reconstruction, Welding, Examination and Testing, and Annexes see the following sections of
the basic document: S.10 through S.13 for austenitic stainless steel, and X.10 through X.13 for duplex stainless steel
components.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=2>>Annex X
(normative)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=2>>Duplex Stainless Steel Storage Tanks<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.1 Scope<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.1.1  This annex covers the inspection, repair, alteration and reconstruction of duplex stainless steel tanks that
were constructed in accordance with API 650, Annex X.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.1.2  This annex states only the requirements that differ from the basic rules in this Standard. For requirements not
stated, the basic rules shall be followed.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.2 References<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>No changes to Section 2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.3 Definitions<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>No changes to Section 3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.4 Suitability for Service<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.4.1  In 4.2.4.1, the requirements of API 650, Section X.3.6 shall also be satisfied.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>X.4.2  In 4.2.4.3, the requirements of API 650, Annex M requirements shall be satisfied for duplex stainless steel
tanks with design temperatures over 40 °C (100 °F) as modified by API 650, X.3.7.2 thru X.3.7.5.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.4.3  In 4.3.3.1, the maximum allowable stress S shall be calculated the same way as for carbon steel.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.4.3.1  Y  = specified minimum yield strength of the plate at design temperature; use material S32304 properties if
duplex material/specification is not known.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.4.3.2  T = specified minimum tensile strength of the plate at design temperature; use material S32304 properties if
duplex material/specification is not known.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.4.4  Table 4-2 shall be in accordance with API 650, Table X-3. When the radiography schedule applied to the
existing weld is unknown; the joint efficiency of 0.7 shall be used.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.4.5  4.3.3.5c, shall be changed to read “Operation at temperatures over 40 °C (100 °F).”<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.4.6  The rules of 4.3.4 for riveted tanks do not cover duplex stainless steel tanks.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.5 Brittle Fracture Considerations<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.5.1  In 5.3.2 the applicable API 650 edition and addendum for duplex stainless steel tanks is 11th edition,
Addendum 1 or later.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.5.2  5.3.5 does not apply to duplex stainless steel tanks.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>X.5.3  The rules of 5.3.8 shall be replaced with the following: Tanks constructed of duplex stainless steels whose
toughness testing or testing exemption conformed to API 650, X.2.3.2 may be considered to be adequately tough for
continued operation.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>X.10 Dismantling and Reconstruction<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.10.1  In 10.4.2, welding shall also meet the requirements of API 650, Section X.4.11.<<HEADING_END>>

X.9.1, for certain dismantling operations.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.10.3  The storage requirements of API 650, Section X.4.2 shall be met.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.10.4  When specified by the Purchaser the requirements of API 650, Section X.4.5 shall be met.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>X.11 Welding<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Welding shall also meet the requirements of API 650, Sections X.4.11 and X.4.12.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>X.12.2  In 12.3, the quality of test water shall meet API 650, Section X.4.10.<<HEADING_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>Annex F, NDE Requirements Summary; any reference to magnetic particle method shall be replaced with the liquid
penetrant method.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
